Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">21</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">17850</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17860</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.8b02000</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D17850-17860%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26issue%3D21%26author%3DQ.%2BLi%26author%3DR.%2BDang%26author%3DM.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BLee%26author%3DZ.%2BHu%26author%3DX.%2BXiao%26title%3DSynthesis%2Bmethod%2Bfor%2Blong%2Bcycle%2Blife%2Blithium-ion%2Bcathode%2Bmaterial%253A%2BNickel-rich%2Bcore%25E2%2580%2593shell%2BLiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.8b02000&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c07504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.8b02000&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis Method for Long Cycle Life Lithium-Ion Cathode Material: Nickel-Rich Core-Shell LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Qi; Dang, Rongbin; Chen, Minmin; Lee, Yulin; Hu, Zhongbo; Xiao, Xiaoling</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17850-17860</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-Ni materials with core-shell structures, whose bulk is rich in Ni content and the outer shell is rich in Mn content, have been demonstrated to improve cycle stability.  The high-Ni cathode material LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2 is a very promising material for Li-ion batteries; however, its low rate performance and esp. cycle performance currently hamper further commercialization.  This study presents a new synthesis method to prep. this core-shell material (LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2@x[Li-Mn-O], x = 0.01, 0.03, 0.06).  Electrochem. data show that LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2@x[Li-Mn-O] (x = 0.03, CS-0.03) exhibits the best high-rate performance, cycle stability, and thermal stability.  The initial discharge capacity of the core-shell sample CS-0.03 is 118 mAh g-1, which is almost the same as the discharge capacity of pristine LiNi0.8Mn0.1Co0.1O2 (117 mAh g-1) at the rate of 10 C in the voltage range of 3.0-4.3 V.  Notably the capacity decay of CS-0.03 is 18.4% after 200 cycles compared to 27% decay in capacity of the pristine sample.  Also, CS-0.03 exhibits better thermal cycling stability.  The capacity retention of the CS-0.03 sample reached 65.1% which is over 1.3 times than that of the pristine 1, whose capacity retention is 49.2% after 105 cycles (55°).  Evidently, the core-shell structured CS-0.03 sample has excellent cycle stability and this synthesis method can be applied to other cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref2" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee01598b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Etacheri, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marom, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Elazari, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Salitra, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aurbach, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Challenges in the development of advanced Li-ion batteries: a review</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">9</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3243</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3262</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c1ee01598b</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D3243-3262%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26issue%3D9%26author%3DV.%2BEtacheri%26author%3DR.%2BMarom%26author%3DR.%2BElazari%26author%3DG.%2BSalitra%26author%3DD.%2BAurbach%26title%3DChallenges%2Bin%2Bthe%2Bdevelopment%2Bof%2Badvanced%2BLi-ion%2Bbatteries%253A%2Ba%2Breview%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc1ee01598b&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c07504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc1ee01598b&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Challenges in the development of advanced Li-ion batteries: a review</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Etacheri, Vinodkumar; Marom, Rotem; Elazari, Ran; Salitra, Gregory; Aurbach, Doron</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3243-3262</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Li-ion battery technol. has become very important in recent years as these batteries show great promise as power sources that can lead us to the elec. vehicle (EV) revolution.  The development of new materials for Li-ion batteries is the focus of research in prominent groups in the field of materials science throughout the world.  Li-ion batteries can be considered to be the most impressive success story of modern electrochem. in the last two decades.  They power most of today's portable devices, and seem to overcome the psychol. barriers against the use of such high energy d. devices on a larger scale for more demanding applications, such as EV.  Since this field is advancing rapidly and attracting an increasing no. of researchers, it is important to provide current and timely updates of this constantly changing technol.  In this review, we describe the key aspects of Li-ion batteries: the basic science behind their operation, the most relevant components, anodes, cathodes, electrolyte solns., as well as important future directions for R&amp;D of advanced Li-ion batteries for demanding use, such as EV and load-leveling applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c25262"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Roy, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Banerjee, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ogale, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Search for new anode materials for high performance Li-ion batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">18</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">20326</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">20348</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.1c25262</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D20326-20348%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26issue%3D18%26author%3DK.%2BRoy%26author%3DA.%2BBanerjee%26author%3DS.%2BOgale%26title%3DSearch%2Bfor%2Bnew%2Banode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bhigh%2Bperformance%2BLi-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.1c25262&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c07504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.1c25262&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Search for new anode materials for high performance Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Roy, Kingshuk; Banerjee, Abhik; Ogale, Satishchandra</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20326-20348</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Owing to an unmatched combination of power and energy d. along with cyclic stability, the Li-ion battery has qualified itself to be the highest performing rechargeable battery.  Taking both transportable and stationary energy storage requirements into consideration, Li-ion batteries indeed stand tall in comparison to any other existing rechargeable battery technologies.  However, graphite, which is still one of the best performing Li-ion anodes, has specific drawbacks in fulfilling the ever-increasing energy and power d. requirements of the modern world.  Therefore, further research on alternative anode materials is absolutely essential.  Equally important is the search for and enhanced use of right earth abundant materials for battery electrodes so as to bring down the costs of the battery systems.  In this spotlight article, we discuss the current research progress in the area of alternative anode materials for Li-ion battery, putting our own research work over the past several years into perspective.  Starting from conversion anode systems like oxides and sulfides, to insertion cum alloying systems like transition metal carbides, to molecularly engineered open framework systems like metal org. frameworks (MOFs), covalent org. frameworks (COFs), and org.-inorg. hybrid perovskites (OIHPs), this spotlight provides a complete essence of the recent developments in the area of alternative anodes.  The possible and potential impact of these new anode materials is detailed and discussed here.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C6CS00776G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span>. <i>Chem.         (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA07392A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Belharouak, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A comprehensive study of the role of transition metals in O3-type layered Na[Ni<sub>x</sub>Co<sub>y</sub>Mn<sub>z</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> (x = 1/3, 0.5, 0.6, and 0.8) cathodes for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molten-Salt Synthesis of O3-Type Layered Oxide Single Crystal Cathodes with Controlled Morphology towards Long-Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lamb, Julia; Jarvis, Karalee; Manthiram, Arumugam</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium layered oxides show great promise as affordable alternatives to lithium layered oxides, but their poor cycle life and air stability limit their practical potential.  Micron-scale single crystals with greater packing d. and lower surface area can overcome these challenges and improve performance compared to the traditional polycryst. morphol.  Herein, the authors present the synthesis of layered O3-type Na(Ni0.3Fe0.4Mn0.3)O2 single-crystals with greatly improved cycle life and air stability.  A molten-salt synthesis technique is adopted with excess sodium hydroxide to obtain platelet-like single crystals.  Because the main mechanisms of both capacity fade and air degrdn. occur as a result of surface reactions at the opening of the sodium diffusion channels, particle morphol. is found to be a crit. metric for materials performance.  More important than particle size or total surface area, the smaller proportion of exposed edge planes in the platelet morphol. greatly reduces the amt. of harmful surface reactions.  Furthermore, the molten-salt method is found to eliminate the need for copptd. precursors and even form better morphol., starting from metal oxides instead of copptd. hydroxides.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref10" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.07.042"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A phase-transition-free cathode for sodium-ion batteries with ultralong cycle life</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>52</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">88</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">94</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phase-transition-free cathode for sodium-ion batteries with ultralong cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Kezhu; Xu, Sheng; Guo, Shaohua; Zhang, Xiaoyu; Zhang, Xueping; Qiao, Yu; Fang, Tiancheng; Wang, Peng; He, Ping; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Sodium-ion-battery, using the layered oxide material as cathodes coupled with carbon anodes, has been proposed for utilization in practice long time ago.  However, the prevailing layered oxides is still hindered by serious phase transition and vol. strain upon sodium release.  Herein, we show a novel copper doped layered P_1 manganese-based oxide material (NCM) with unique bulk and nanoscale Na-free surface structures as a sodium host to overcome the above limitation.  Our research disclosed this P_1 NCM material has a wide phase-transition-free zone between 2 V and 4.5 V with a tiny lattice vol. change upon cycling.  Besides, it delivers an excellent chem. stability during humid air exposure.  In contrast to most environmentally sensitive layered materials, after aging for 60 days in humid air, P_1 NCM still exhibits the superior cycling performance (95.8% capacity retention after 1000 cycles) and excellent rate capability as well as an outstanding sodium storage performance in full cells.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref11" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1088/2515-7639/abf545"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kendrick, E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent progress on strategies to improve the high-voltage stability of layered-oxide cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                 10.1039/C5RA08321D</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D53129-53154%26journal%3DRSC%2BAdv.%26issue%3D65%26author%3DM.%2BSawicki%26author%3DL.%2BL.%2BShaw%26title%3DAdvances%2Band%2Bchallenges%2Bof%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%2Bas%2Bpost%2Blithium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC5RA08321D&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c07504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC5RA08321D&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advances and challenges of sodium ion batteries as post lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sawicki, Monica; Shaw, Leon L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">65</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">53129-53154</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2046-2069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy and climate concerns have made the need for research towards elec. energy storage.  In this context, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have attracted significant attention lately.  Sodium is an abundant resource that is low cost and safe which makes it an attractive alternative to lithium.  Its chem. properties are similar to that of Li which makes the transition into using Na chem. for ion battery systems feasible.  This review focuses on the latest progress in both cathode and anode materials for SIBs.  It also details research in binders and additives and their effects on the SIB system.  It further highlights the optimization of org. electrolytes and ionic liq. based electrolytes for utilization in SIBs.  The mechanisms of sodium ion storage, transport, and solid electrolyte interphase formation are also discussed to better understand the behavior of ions and battery materials during de/intercalation.  Finally, personal perspectives on outlook and major challenges ahead for SIBs are offered.  These comprehensive and in-depth discussions along with proposed directions can enlighten ideas and offer avenues in the rational design of durable and high performance SIBs in the near future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.227064"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeong, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, W.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">O3-type NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> layered cathode for Na-ion batteries: Structural evolution and redox mechanism upon Na (de) intercalation</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.227064</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D439%26publication_year%3D2019%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DM.%2BJeong%26author%3DH.%2BLee%26author%3DJ.%2BYoon%26author%3DW.-S.%2BYoon%26title%3DO3-type%2BNaNi1%252F3Fe1%252F3Mn1%252F3O2%2Blayered%2Bcathode%2Bfor%2BNa-ion%2Bbatteries%253A%2BStructural%2Bevolution%2Band%2Bredox%2Bmechanism%2Bupon%2BNa%2B%2528de%2529%2Bintercalation%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2019.227064&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c07504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2019.227064&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">O3-type NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 layered cathode for Na-ion batteries: Structural evolution and redox mechanism upon Na (de) intercalation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jeong, Mihee; Lee, Hayeon; Yoon, Jaesang; Yoon, Won-Sub</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">439</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">227064</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered sodium-ion battery cathode, O3-type NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2, has been systematically investigated by synchrotron-based analyses to characterize the structural behavior during electrochem. reaction.  X-ray absorption spectroscopy shows reversible redox process upon cycling and clearly proves that both Ni and Fe are active in Na1-xNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 and that redox couples of Ni2+/Ni4+via Ni3+ and Fe3+/Fe4+ are responsible for charge compensation.  Specifically, the capacity is mainly realized with Ni2+/Ni4+ and slightly from Fe3+/Fe4+ under charging voltage of 4.0 V.  At high voltage (&gt;4.0 V), however, Fe redox reaction is dominant and Ni contributes slightly to capacity.  In structural evolution, Na1-xNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 undergoes phase transformation from O3 to P3 phase below 4.0 V and further reaches OP2 structure above 4.0 V along with a significant contraction of d-spacing.  Moreover, quant. anal. of extended X-ray absorption fine structure suggests that disorder of local structure for Fe is greatly increased in high voltage region.  Accordingly, collapse of d-spacing can be considered as being caused by Fe migration in the TM layer into the neighboring Na layer.  This study thus provides detailed redox behavior and factor of structural distortions under high voltage region by considering bulk and local structural changes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201702024"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The first report on excellent cycling stability and superior rate capability of Na3V2(PO4)3 for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Saravanan, Kuppan; Mason, Chad W.; Rudola, Ashish; Wong, Kim Hai; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">444-450</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are attractive for the rapidly emerging large-scale energy storage market for intermittent renewable resources.  Currently a viable cathode material does not exist for practical non-aq. sodium ion battery applications.  Here we disclose a high performance, durable electrode material based on the 3D NASICON framework.  Porous Na3V2(PO4)3/C was synthesized using a novel soln.-based approach.  This material, as a cathode, is capable of delivering an energy storage capacity of ∼400 mWh/g vs. sodium metal.  Furthermore, at high current rates (10, 20 and 40 C), it displayed remarkable capacity retention.  Equally impressive is the long term cycle life.  Nearly 50% of the initial capacity was retained after 30,000 charge/discharge cycles at 40 C (4.7 A/g).  Notably, coulombic efficiency was 99.68% (av.) over the course of cycling.  To the best of our knowledge, the combination of high energy d., high power d. and ultra long cycle life demonstrated here has never been reported before for sodium ion batteries.  We believe our findings will have profound implications for developing large-scale energy storage systems for renewable energy sources.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1038/s41560-021-00792-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-high-voltage Ni-rich layered cathodes in practical Li metal batteries enabled by a sulfonamide-based electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xue, Weijiang; Huang, Mingjun; Li, Yutao; Zhu, Yun Guang; Gao, Rui; Xiao, Xianghui; Zhang, Wenxu; Li, Sipei; Xu, Guiyin; Yu, Yang; Li, Peng; Lopez, Jeffrey; Yu, Daiwei; Dong, Yanhao; Fan, Weiwei; Shi, Zhe; Xiong, Rui; Sun, Cheng-Jun; Hwang, Inhui; Lee, Wah-Keat; Shao-Horn, Yang; Johnson, Jeremiah A.; Li, Ju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">495-505</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANFD</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Portfolio</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">By increasing the charging voltage, a cell specific energy of &gt;400 W h kg-1 is achievable with LiNi0.8Mn0.1Co0.1O2 in Li metal batteries.  However, stable cycling of high-nickel cathodes at ultra-high voltages is extremely challenging.  Here we report that a rationally designed sulfonamide-based electrolyte enables stable cycling of com. LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2 with a cut-off voltage up to 4.7 V in Li metal batteries.  In contrast to com. carbonate electrolytes, the electrolyte not only suppresses side reactions, stress-corrosion cracking, transition-metal dissoln. and impedance growth on the cathode side, but also enables highly reversible Li metal stripping and plating leading to a compact morphol. and low pulverization.  Our lithium-metal battery delivers a specific capacity &gt;230 mA h g-1 and an av. Coulombic efficiency &gt;99.65% over 100 cycles.  Even under harsh testing conditions, the 4.7 V lithium-metal battery can retain &gt;88% capacity for 90 cycles, advancing practical lithium-metal batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.8b04418"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Besli, M.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoscale Chemomechanical Interplay of the LiNi0.8Co0.15Al0.05O2 Cathode in Solid-State Polymer Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Besli, Munir M.; Xia, Sihao; Kuppan, Saravanan; Huang, Yiqing; Metzger, Michael; Shukla, Alpesh Khushalchand; Schneider, Gerhard; Hellstrom, Sondra; Christensen, Jake; Doeff, Marca M.; Liu, Yijin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">31</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">491-501</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Complex chemomech. interplay exists over a wide range of length scales within the hierarchically structured lithium-ion battery.  At the mesoscale, the interdependent structural complexity and chem. heterogeneity collectively govern the local chem. and, as a result, critically affect the cell level performance.  Here the morphol. and state are investigated of charge (SOC) inhomogeneity within secondary NCA particles that were cycled in solid polymer batteries.  Substantial inhomogeneity is obsd. in the nickel oxidn. state (a proxy for SOC) and loss of structural integrity within secondary particles after only 20 cycles due to significant intergranular cracking.  The formation of mesoscale cracks causes loss of ionic and elec. contact within cathode particles, triggering increases in local impedance and rearrangement of transport pathways for charge carriers.  This can eventually lead to deactivation of subparticle level domains in solid-state lithium-ion batteries.  The findings highlight the importance of proper mesoscale strain and defect management in polymer lithium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202400569"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kumar, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ming, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphic, Quantitation, Visualization, Standardization, Digitization, and Intelligence of Electrolyte and Electrolyte-Electrode Interface</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte Solvation Structure Design for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tian, Zhengnan; Zou, Yeguo; Liu, Gang; Wang, Yizhou; Yin, Jian; Ming, Jun; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  In the past two decades, exploring new electrolytes for SIBs has generally relied on the "solid electrolyte interphase (SEI)" theory to optimize the electrolyte components.  However, many obsd. phenomena cannot be fully explained by the SEI theory.  Therefore, electrolyte solvation structure and electrode-electrolyte interface behavior have recently received tremendous research interest to explain the improved performance.  Considering there is currently no review paper focusing on the solvation structure of electrolytes in SIBs, a systematic survey on SIBs is provided, in which the specific solvation structure design guidelines and their consequent impact on the electrochem. performance are elucidated.  The key driving force of solvation structure formation, and the recent advances in adjusting SIB solvation structures are discussed in detail.  It is believed that this review can provide new insights into the electrolyte optimization strategies of high-performance SIBs and even other emerging battery systems.  Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are considered the most promising battery technol. in the post-lithium era due to the abundant sodium reserves.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201803963"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Radially Oriented Single-Crystal Primary Nanosheets Enable Ultrahigh Rate and Cycling Properties of LiNi<sub>0.8</sub>Co<sub>0.1</sub>Mn<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode Material for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Between Scylla and Charybdis: Balancing Among Structural Stability and Energy Density of Layered NCM Cathode Materials for Advanced Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">de Biasi, Lea; Kondrakov, Aleksandr O.; Gesswein, Holger; Brezesinski, Torsten; Hartmann, Pascal; Janek, Juergen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">121</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">26163-26171</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two major strategies are currently pursued to improve the energy d. of Li-ion batteries using LiNixCoyMnzO2 (NCM) cathode materials.  One is to increase the fraction of redox active Ni (≥80%), which allows larger amts. of Li to be extd. at a given cutoff voltage (Umax).  The other is to increase Umax, in particular for medium-Ni content NCM materials.  However, the accompanying lattice changes ultimately lead to capacity fading in both cases.  Here the structural changes occurring in Li1.02NixCoyMnzO2 (with x = 1/3, 0.5, 0.6, 0.7, 0.8 and 0.85) during cycling operation in the voltage range between 3.0 and 4.6 V vs. Li are quantified by operando x-ray diffraction combined with detailed Rietveld anal.  All samples show a large decrease in unit cell vol. upon charging, ranging from 2.4% for NCM111 (33% Ni) to 8.0% for NCM851005 (85% Ni).  To make a fair comparison of the structural stability of the different NCM materials, energy densities as a function of Umax are estd. and correlated with x-ray diffraction results.  NCMs with a lower Ni content allow for specific energies similar to that of, e.g., Ni-rich NCM811 (80% Ni) when operated at sufficiently high Umax, but still undergo less pronounced changes in structure.  Nevertheless, as indicated by charge/discharge tests, the capacity retention of low- and medium-Ni content NCMs cycled to high Umax is also strongly affected by factors other than stability of the layered crystal lattice (electrolyte decompn. etc.).  Overall, the complexity of the degrdn. processes needs to be better understood to identify optimal cycling conditions for specific cathode compns.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b06701"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guiming, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">McDonald, M.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into the Effects of Zinc Doping on Structural Phase Transition of P2-Type Sodium Nickel Manganese Oxide Cathodes for High-Energy Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xuehang; Xu, Gui-Liang; Zhong, Guiming; Gong, Zhengliang; McDonald, Matthew J.; Zheng, Shiyao; Fu, Riqiang; Chen, Zonghai; Amine, Khalil; Yang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22227-22237</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type sodium nickel manganese oxide-based cathode materials with higher energy densities are prime candidates for applications in rechargeable sodium ion batteries.  A systematic study combining in situ high energy X-ray diffraction (HEXRD), ex situ X-ray absorption fine spectroscopy (XAFS), transmission electron microscopy (TEM), and solid-state NMR (SS-NMR) techniques was carried out to gain a deep insight into the structural evolution of P2-Na0.66Ni0.33-xZnxMn0.67O2 (x = 0, 0.07) during cycling.  In situ HEXRD and ex situ TEM measurements indicate that an irreversible phase transition occurs upon sodium insertion-extn. of Na0.66Ni0.33Mn0.67O2.  Zinc doping of this system results in a high structural reversibility.  XAFS measurements indicate that both materials are almost completely dependent on the Ni4+/Ni3+/Ni2+ redox couple to provide charge/discharge capacity.  SS-NMR measurements indicate that both reversible and irreversible migration of transition metal ions into the sodium layer occurs in the material at the fully charged state.  The irreversible migration of transition metal ions triggers a structural distortion, leading to the obsd. capacity and voltage fading.  Our results allow a new understanding of the importance of improving the stability of transition metal layers.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref24" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.03.031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, T.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bae, I. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>422</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">8</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.03.031</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D422%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D1-8%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DT.-Y.%2BYu%26author%3DJ.-Y.%2BHwang%26author%3DI.%2BT.%2BBae%26author%3DH.-G.%2BJung%26author%3DY.-K.%2BSun%26title%3DHigh-performance%2BTi-doped%2BO3-type%2BNa%255BTix%2528Ni0.6Co0.2Mn0.2%25291-x%255DO2%2Bcathodes%2Bfor%2Bpractical%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2019.03.031&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c07504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2019.03.031&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-performance Ti-doped O3-type Na[Tix(Ni0.6Co0.2Mn0.2)1-x]O2 cathodes for practical sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Tae-Yeon; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Bae, In Tae; Jung, Hun-Gi; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">422</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1-8</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ti-doped O3-type Na[Tix(Ni0.6Co0.2Mn0.2)1-x]O2 is studied as a high-performance cathode material for practical sodium-ion batteries.  The effect of partial Ti doping on the structural and electrochem. properties of O3-type Na[Ni0.6Co0.2Mn0.2]O2 materials is investigated by varying the Ti content (x) in Na[Ni0.6Co0.2Mn0.2]O2 from 0 to 0.01 to 0.03.  SEM images show that upon doping, the primary particles aggregate and form densely packed secondary particles, yielding enhanced mech. strength and high tap d. of ∼2.3 g cm-3.  The compact morphol. of the particles effectively minimizes the void vol. for possible electrolyte penetration that usually leads to unwanted side reactions.  In addn., partial doping of Ti in the transition-metal layer greatly improve the structural stability.  By taking both morphol. and structural advantages, the O3-type Na[Ti0.03(Ni0.6Co0.2Mn0.2)0.97]O2 cathode demonstrate the great enhancements of battery performances in terms of capacity, cycle retention, rate capability, and thermal properties.  Pouch-type full cells assembled by combining the present cathodes with hard carbon anodes show good practical applicability, with an outstanding cycle retention of 77% over 400 cycles.  The results of this study may open up a new avenue for designing and developing suitable transition metal oxide cathodes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.06.026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Enaya, H.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered P2-Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 as high-voltage cathode for sodium-ion batteries: The capacity decay mechanism and Al2O3 surface modification</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Fang, Xin; Zhang, Anyi; Shen, Chenfei; Liu, Qingzhou; Enaya, Hani A.; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">27-34</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The P2 type Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 is a high-voltage cathode material for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 173 mA h/g and a long operation voltage plateau of 4.2 V.  However, the material has exhibited unstable cycling performance within the high-voltage window, which severely limits its application.  Moreover, its capacity decay mechanism is still unclear.  In this study, we first investigate the difference between as-prepd. and after-cycling Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 samples, and then confirmed that the transition metal oxide layer exfoliation assocd. with the crystal phase transition during Na ion extn. and insertion is the main cause of capacity fading.  The Al2O3 coated Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 with enhanced cycling performance was prepd. by taking the benefit of Al2O3 coating.  The Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 sample without any surface modification presented a 164 mA h/g initial specific discharge capacity within the voltage window from 2.5 V to 4.3 V, and the capacity decayed to 44 mA h/g at the 300th cycle, resulting in only a 26.8% retention.  In contrast, the Al2O3-coated Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 presented a similar initial capacity, but with an enhanced 73.2% retention after 300 cycles.  The enhanced cycling stability obsd. in after-cycling characterization and anal. confirms that the Al2O3 surface coating can effectively suppress the unfavorable side reaction at high voltage and the exfoliation of the metal oxide layers.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201400458"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miller, D.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Surface regulation enables high stability of single-crystal lithium-ion cathodes at high voltage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Fang; Lou, Shuaifeng; Li, Shuang; Yu, Zhenjiang; Liu, Qingsong; Dai, Alvin; Cao, Chuntian; Toney, Michael F.; Ge, Mingyuan; Xiao, Xianghui; Lee, Wah-Keat; Yao, Yudong; Deng, Junjing; Liu, Tongchao; Tang, Yiping; Yin, Geping; Lu, Jun; Su, Dong; Wang, Jiajun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3050</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Single-crystal cathode materials for lithium-ion batteries have attracted increasing interest in providing greater capacity retention than their polycryst. counterparts.  However, after being cycled at high voltages, these single-crystal materials exhibit severe structural instability and capacity fade.  Understanding how the surface structural changes det. the performance degrdn. over cycling is crucial, but remains elusive.  Here, we investigate the correlation of the surface structure, internal strain, and capacity deterioration by using operando X-ray spectroscopy imaging and nano-tomog.  We directly observe a close correlation between surface chem. and phase distribution from homogeneity to heterogeneity, which induces heterogeneous internal strain within the particle and the resulting structural/performance degrdn. during cycling.  We also discover that surface chem. can significantly enhance the cyclic performance.  Our modified process effectively regulates the performance fade issue of single-crystal cathode and provides new insights for improved design of high-capacity battery materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.coelec.2021.100831"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Single-crystal high-nickel layered cathodes for lithium-ion batteries: advantages, mechanism, challenges and approaches</span>. <i>Curr.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Single-crystal high-nickel layered cathodes for lithium-ion batteries: advantages, mechanism, challenges and approaches</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zeng, Weihao; Xia, Fanjie; Tian, Weixi; Cao, Fei; Chen, Junxin; Wu, Jinsong; Song, Rongguo; Mu, Shichun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Current Opinion in Electrochemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The ever-increasing demand of advanced lithium-ion batteries is calling for high-performance cathode materials.  Among promising next-generation cathode materials, high-nickel layered oxides with spherical polycryst. secondary particles exhibit the outstanding advantage of high energy d.  However, polycrystals, suffered from the pulverization of particles and the expansion of cracks, show the shortcoming of poor cycling performance.  As an efficient soln., the single-crystal route has been underestimated hitherto.  Herein, the unique structural degrdn. mechanism of single crystals is emphasized, and their advantages against polycrystals are comprehensively summarized in terms of electrochem., thermal, and mech. properties.  Furthermore, we point out the practical challenges of single-crystal materials toward practical applications and raise hopeful strategies for overcoming such issues.  Based on the aforementioned characteristics and approaches, future directions are outlooked as well.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.202100234"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Progress of Single-Crystal Nickel-Rich Cathode Materials for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2100234</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Research Progress of Single-Crystal Nickel-Rich Materials for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">You, Bianzheng; Wang, Zhixing; Shen, Fang; Chang, Yijiao; Peng, Wenjie; Li, Xinhai; Guo, Huajun; Hu, Qiyang; Deng, Chengwei; Yang, Sheng; Yan, Guochun; Wang, Jiexi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Single-crystal nickel-rich cathode materials (SC-NRCMs) are the most promising candidates for next-generation power batteries which enable longer driving range and reliable safety.  In this , the outstanding advantages of SC-NRCMs are discussed systematically in aspects of structural and thermal stabilities.  Particularly, the intergranular-crack-free morphol. exhibits superior cycling performance and negligible parasitic reactions even under severe conditions.  Besides, various synthetic methods are summarized and the relation between precursor, sintering process, and final single-crystal products are revealed, providing a full view of synthetic methods.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Eutectic salt-assisted planetary centrifugal deagglomeration for single-crystalline cathode synthesis</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yoon, Moonsu; Dong, Yanhao; Huang, Yimeng; Wang, Baoming; Kim, Junghwa; Park, Jin-Sung; Hwang, Jaeseong; Park, Jaehyun; Kang, Seok Ju; Cho, Jaephil; Li, Ju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Single-cryst. layered cathodes are often desirable for advanced lithium-ion batteries.  However, constrained by the accessible temp. range to prevent lithium evapn., lattice defects and particle agglomerations, the prodn. of single-cryst. cathodes with high phase purity, good electrochem. performance and scalability remains challenging.  Here we invent a new mechanochem. activation process that offers a general soln. to the conundrum of synthesizing coarse single-crystal cathodes with Li-/Mn-rich or Ni-rich chem., which differs from the equipment- and energy-intense and long-duration mechanochem. routes that are difficult to scale up.  Our approach is based on interfacial reactive wetting, mediated by transient eutectic salts in situ melted by moderate mech. agitations, to form a colloidal suspension of nanosized oxides dispersed in liquified lithium salts.  It efficiently deagglomerates the polycryst. precursors, repacks the crystals and homogenizes the lithium-salt distribution, thus enabling facile particle coarsening later into the single-cryst. morphol. with improved electrochem. performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.139431"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Design and mechanism exploration of single-crystalline NCM811 materials with superior comprehensive performance for Li-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design and mechanism exploration of single-crystalline NCM811 materials with superior comprehensive performance for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Xiangbang; Yang, Huiya; Zhang, Yige; Dai, Pengpeng; Tang, Yonglin; Zeng, Jing; Zhao, Jinbao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although single-cryst. LiNixCoyMn1-x-yO2 (SC NCM) materials have been confirmed to have advantages in cycle performance, storage performance and thermal stability, the comprehensive performance of SC NCM materials is not perfect enough nowadays.  And the current research on the modification mostly focuses on polycryst. NCM materials, the modification of SC NCM materials is rare.  Therefore, the synthesis and modification of SC NCM materials deserve special attention.  In this work, the SC high-nickel LiNi0.8Co0.1Mn0.1O2 (NCM811) is modified by doping with titanium (Ti) element.  The doped material can maintain better structural stability, and suppress the side reaction between the material interface and the electrolyte, so the cycling performance is significantly improved.  Doping enlarges the transport channel of Li+ in the material, thereby increasing the rate property.  The lattice slip phenomenon of the modified material under high voltage is significantly suppressed, and the oxygen release and the reactivity with the electrolyte at high temp. of the material after delithiation are reduced, so the high voltage resistance and thermal stability are significantly enhanced.  In conclusion, the comprehensive properties of SC NCM811 materials are improved by doping, and detailed mechanism study is carried out, which can provide ref. for the further modification of SC NCM materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/0921-4526(93)90108-I"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rodríguez-Carvajal, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent advances in magnetic structure determination by neutron powder diffraction</span>. <i>Phys.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The irreversible consumption of sodium at the anode side during the first cycle prominently reduces the energy d. of Na-ion batteries.  Different sacrificial cathode additives have been recently reported to address this problem; however, crit. issues such as byproducts (e.g., CO2) release during cycling and incompatibility with current battery fabrication procedures potentially deteriorate the full-cell performance and prevent the practical application.  Herein, an additive-free self-presodiation strategy is proposed to create lattice-coherent but component-dependent O3-NaxTMMnO2 (TM = transition metal ion(s)) cathodes by a quenching treatment rather than the general natural cooling.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The ever-increasing energy d. requirements in elec. vehicles (EVs) have boosted the development of Ni-rich layered oxide cathodes for state-of-the-art lithium-ion batteries.  Nevertheless, the commercialization of polycryst. Ni-rich cathodes (PCNCs) is hindered by the severe performance degrdn. and safety concerns that are tightly related to its particle cracking during cycling.  Single-cryst. Ni-rich cathodes (SCNCs) with eliminated grain boundaries and high mech. strength have recently attracted extensive attention owing to their superior structural and cycling stability, which present high crack resistance during electrochem. operation.  Various articles have focused on the trial-and-error synthesis and modifications of SCNCs, as well as the comparison of performances and mechanisms with PCNCs.  However, there has been much less effort in systematic anal. and summary to reveal their key challenges, controversies, and the corresponding primary causes.  In this review, the advantages and debates in structural and electrochem. properties of SCNCs over PCNCs are summarized to provide fundamental understanding of SCNCs.  Then the current practical issues and challenges are comprehensively discussed from the viewpoints of both academia and industry, as well as the proposed modification strategies and underlying mechanisms for SCNCs.  The outlook and perspectives are further given to facilitate the com. applications of SCNCs in high-performance EVs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2021.138982"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Truong, B.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The effect of lithium-excess on Ni-rich LiNi0.6Co0.2Mn0.2O2 cathode materials prepared by a Taylor flow reactor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Truong, BeTa Thi; Wu, Yi-Shiuan; Hung, Tai-Feng; Chien, Wen-Chen; Wu, She-Huang; Jose, Rajan; Lue, Shingjiang Jessie; Yang, Chun-Chen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study we investigated the effect of the Li-excess on electrochem. properties of LixNi0.6Co0.2Mn0.2O2 cathode materials, which was obtained by sintering Ni0.6Co0.2Mn0.2(OH)2 with a various amts. of LiOH (samples with Li-excesses of 5, 10, 20, and 25 mol% are denoted herein as NCM-5, NCM-10, NCM-20, and NCM-25, resp.).  The LixNi0.6Co0.2Mn0.2O2 samples retained their excellent cryst. ordering in the rhombohedral layered structure, with the space group R3-m.  When the Li-excess increased, Rietveld refinement revealed that cation mixing occurred, the lattice parameters decreased, the transition metal slab thickness increased, and the inter-slab Li space thickness decreased.  Nevertheless, an appropriate degree of cation mixing could retain the structural stability and improve the rate capability of the electrodes.  It was found that the sample contg. the 20 mol% Li-excess (NCM-20) achieved the best cyclic stability, with a capacity retention of 90% at a current rate of 1C/1C for 200 cycles between 2.8 and 4.5 V at room temp.  In situ X-ray diffraction confirmed the greater stability of the crystal phase and phys. structure of NCM-20 upon initial cycling.  In operando microcalorimetry revealed that the thermal stability of NCM-20 was greater than that of the other cathode materials; it exhibited markedly less heat-generated flux and prevented thermal runaway.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA01593J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kimijima, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zettsu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yubuta, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hirata, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kami, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Teshima, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Molybdate flux growth of idiomorphic Li(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Co<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub> single crystals and characterization of their capabilities as cathode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Journal of Materials Chemistry A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">19</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">7289</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7296</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-energy O3-Na1-2xCax[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 cathodes for long-life sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Tae-Yeon; Kim, Jongsoon; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Kim, Hyungsub; Han, Geumjae; Jung, Hun-Gi; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To facilitate the practical realization of sodium-ion batteries, the energy d., detd. by the output operating voltage and/or capacity, needs to be improved to the level of com. Li-ion batteries.  Herein, O3-type Na0.98Ca0.01[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 is synthesized by incorporating Ca2+ into the NaO6 octahedron of Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 and its potential use as a cathode material for high energy d. SIBs is demonstrated.  The ionic radius of calcium (≈1.00 Å) is similar to that of sodium (≈1.02 Å); hence, it is energetically favorable for calcium to occupy sites in the sodium layers.  Within a wide operating voltage range of 2.0-4.3 V, O3-type Na0.98Ca0.01[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 exhibits a reversible O3-P3-O3 phase transition with small vol. changes compared to Ca-free Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 because of the strong interaction between Ca2+ and O2- and delivers a high reversible capacity of 209 mA h g-1 at 15 mA g-1 with improved cycling stability.  Moreover, Ca substitution improves the practically useful aspects such as thermal and air stability.  A prototype pouch full cell with a hard carbon anode shows an excellent capacity retention of 67% over 300 cycles.  Thus, this study provides an efficient and simple method to boost the performance and applicability of layered oxide cathode materials for practical applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702028"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cha, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prospect and Reality of Ni-Rich Cathode for Commercialization</span>. <i>Adv. However, the air sensitivity of this material limits practical application and is not well understood.  Here, the authors present a detailed study of NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 powders stored in different atms. (O, Ar, and CO2), either dry or wet.  X-ray diffraction and FTIR measurements were used to characterize the materials and their surface species before and after controlled-atm. storage.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure and electrochemistry of lithium cobalt oxide synthesized at 400°C</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gummow, R.     </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel LiCoO2 compd. has been prepd. by the reaction of Li2CO3 and CoCO3 at 400°.  Unlike the well-known LiCoO2 structure that is synthesized at higher temp. (900°) and contains Li+ and Co3+ ions in discrete layers between planes of close-packed oxygen ions, the structure of LiCoO2 (400°) has approx. 6% cobalt within the lithium layers.  The electrochem. properties of LiCoO2 (400°) differ significantly from LiCoO2 (900°).  Whereas electrochem. extn. from LixCoO2 (900°) in room-temp. lithium cells takes place as a single-phase reaction above 3.9 V for x ≤ 0.9, electrochem. extn. from LixCoO2 (400°) occurs as a two-phase reaction at an open-circuit voltage of 3.61 V for 0.1 &lt; x &lt; 0.95.  Because LixCoO2 (400°) is a less oxidizing material than its high-temp. analog, it is expected to be more stable in many of the org.-based electrolytes that are currently employed in lithium cells.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1039/D2YA00211F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moiseev, I.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simultaneous MgO coating and Mg doping of Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 cathode: facile and customizable approach to high-voltage sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Yu, Tae-Yeon; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, we report substantially improved high-voltage stability of Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 as a cathode material due to a surface MgO coating and bulk Mg doping for high-voltage sodium-ion batteries, for the first time.
